# Task: Implement CSS Container Queries Size Evaluation in Servo

## Objective
Add CSS Container Queries support to Servo's style system, implementing the `@container` at-rule with size-based queries (`min-width`, `max-width`, `min-height`, `max-height`, `width`, `height`).

CSS Container Queries (CSS Containment Level 3) allow elements to be styled based on their container's size rather than the viewport. A container is designated via `container-type: size | inline-size` and queried with `@container (min-width: 400px) { ... }`.

## Requirements

1. **Define container type properties** in Servo's style properties:
   - Add `container-type` CSS property (values: `normal`, `size`, `inline-size`)
   - Add `container-name` CSS property (values: `none` or custom ident)
   - These should be defined in `components/style/properties/` following Servo's property definition pattern

2. **Parse @container rules** in the CSS parser:
   - Extend `components/style/stylesheets/` to handle `@container` at-rules
   - Parse container size conditions: `(min-width: Npx)`, `(max-width: Npx)`, `(width > Npx)`, etc.
   - Store parsed container queries in the stylesheet data structures

3. **Implement container query evaluation**:
   - In the style resolution path, evaluate container size queries against the actual container dimensions
   - Walk up the DOM tree to find the nearest container ancestor with matching `container-name`
   - Compare container dimensions against the query conditions

4. **Integrate with style matching**:
   - During rule matching, check if `@container` rules apply given the current container sizes
   - Rules inside a matching `@container` block should be included in the cascade

## Key Reference Files
- `components/style/properties/longhands/` — longhand property definitions (add container-type, container-name here)
- `components/style/stylesheets/rule_parser.rs` — at-rule parsing
- `components/style/stylesheets/container_rule.rs` — may already exist as a stub
- `components/style/matching.rs` — style matching/cascade logic
- `components/style/values/specified/length.rs` — length value parsing
- `components/style/media_queries/` — reference pattern for conditional rules (similar to @media)

## Success Criteria
- `container-type` property definition exists in properties
- `container-name` property definition exists in properties
- Container query parsing structures defined (ContainerCondition or similar)
- @container at-rule parsing integrated into stylesheet parser
- Size query evaluation logic exists (comparing dimensions against conditions)
- Integration point in style matching that checks container queries

## Tests to write

### 1. `ContainerName` tests
- `none()` creates an empty slice → `is_none()` true
- `parse` with `"none"` → `is_none()` true, serializes as `"none"`
- `parse` with a valid ident → contains that ident, serializes back
- `parse` with multiple idents → serializes as space-separated
- `parse` with disallowed idents like `"not"`, `"or"`, `"and"` → error
- `parse_for_query` with a single valid ident → works
- `parse_for_query` with `"none"` → error (disallowed)
- `parse_for_query` with `"not"`, `"and"`, `"or"` → error (disallowed)
- `parse_for_query` with multiple idents → only parses first (not in for_query mode)
- Roundtrip serialization for single and multi-name values

### 2. `ContainerType` tests
- Bitflag constants: `NORMAL == 0`, `INLINE_SIZE` exists, `SIZE` exists
- `is_normal()`: true for `NORMAL`, false for others
- `is_size_container_type()`: true for `SIZE`, true for `INLINE_SIZE`, false for `NORMAL`
- `SIZE | INLINE_SIZE` is invalid (validate_mixed_flags)
- Parse roundtrip: `"normal"`, `"inline-size"`, `"size"`, `"scroll-state"` (if pref enabled)
- Parse error for mixed: `"size inline-size"`

### 3. `ContainerSizeQuery` tests
- `none()` creates an `Evaluated(ContainerSizeQueryResult::default())` variant
- `get()` on a `none()` query returns the default result
- Can't inspect internal state directly since `ContainerSizeQueryResult` fields are private

### 4. `ContainerConditionId` tests
- `none()` is `ContainerConditionId(0)` → compare two `none()` calls → equal
- Comparison operators (since it derives `Ord`, `PartialOrd`): `none() < ContainerConditionId(1)`

- `(width)` → `Empty` variant → serializes as `(width)` ✓

- `"sidebar (width > 300px)"` should parse name="sidebar", condition="(width > 300px)"

Looking at the ToCss derive for a struct with two fields... In stylo's custom ToCss derive, fields are serialized in order. There's no automatic space insertion between struct fields in the ToCss derive - each field calls `to_css` on itself. So the output would be: `sidebarcondition_output` without a space.

But that doesn't match the CSS spec. Let me look more carefully at what `#[derive(ToCss)]` does for structs...

Actually in the style crate's custom ToCss derive, struct fields are serialized in sequence without spaces. But the `ContainerRule::to_css_with_guard` implementation manually adds the space. The `ContainerCondition` struct has a standalone `ToCss` derive but the rule itself doesn't use it directly for the rule output.

I am thinking...: Now I fully understand `parse_internal`:

When `for_query = false` (i.e., `ContainerName::parse`):
1. Gets first ident
2. If it's "none" → returns `none()`
3. Otherwise checks it's not in DISALLOWED_CONTAINER_NAMES (["none", "not", "or", "and"])
4. Then tries more idents (multiple names allowed in `container-name` property)
5. Returns `ContainerName(idents)`

When `for_query = true` (i.e., `ContainerName::parse_for_query`):
1. Gets first ident
2. NOT "none" → doesn't return early
3. Checks NOT in DISALLOWED_CONTAINER_NAMES (so "none", "not", "or", "and" all fail)
4. No more idents (single name only for queries)
5. Returns `ContainerName([name])`

So for `ContainerName::parse`:
- "none" → parses as `none()` ✓
- "sidebar" → parses as ContainerName(["sidebar"]) ✓
- "sidebar card" → parses as ContainerName(["sidebar", "card"]) ✓
- "not" → `CustomIdent::from_ident` with "not" in DISALLOWED list → error ✓
- "or" → error ✓
- "and" → error ✓

For `ContainerName::parse_for_query`:
- "none" → tries `CustomIdent::from_ident` with "none" in DISALLOWED list → error ✓
- "not" → error ✓
- "and" → error ✓
- "or" → error ✓
- "sidebar" → success ✓

I am thinking...: Now I understand the parse logic:

`parse_internal` with `for_query=true`:
1. Reads first ident
2. Since `for_query=true`, does NOT do the `!for_query && first.eq_ignore_ascii_case("none")` check for returning `Self::none()`
3. Tries to create `CustomIdent::from_ident(location, first, DISALLOWED_CONTAINER_NAMES)` - if first is "none", "not", "or", "and", this will fail with error
4. Since `for_query=true`, does NOT try to parse more idents

So `parse_for_query` rejects: "none", "not", "or", "and" - returning error ✓

`parse_internal` with `for_query=false` (i.e., `ContainerName::parse`):
1. Reads first ident
2. Since `!for_query`, checks if first is "none" → returns `Self::none()`
3. If not "none", tries to create CustomIdent with DISALLOWED_CONTAINER_NAMES → fails for "none","not","or","and" but we already handled "none"
4. Then loops to read more idents

So `ContainerName::parse("none")` → `Self::none()` ✓
`ContainerName::parse("sidebar")` → ContainerName with ["sidebar"] ✓
`ContainerName::parse("sidebar card")` → ContainerName with ["sidebar", "card"] ✓

ToCss for ContainerName:
- `#[css(iterable, if_empty = "none")]`
- Empty → "none"
- One element → "sidebar"
- Two elements → "sidebar card" (space-separated, since it's `iterable`)

For `parse_for_query("sidebar")`:
- first = "sidebar"
- CustomIdent::from_ident(location, "sidebar", DISALLOWED) → Ok(CustomIdent("sidebar"))
- Since `for_query=true`, doesn't loop for more idents
- Returns ContainerName(["sidebar"]) ✓

Now let me think about the ToCss for `ContainerName::parse("sidebar card")`:
- ContainerName(["sidebar", "card"])
- ToCss: iterable with space separator → "sidebar card" ✓
